class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Hip Latin</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://iambeckyg.com">iambeckyg<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Rebbeca Marie Gomez</b><sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21under21_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21under21-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (born March 2, 1997),<sup id="cite_ref-21under21_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21under21-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> known professionally as <b>Becky G</b>, is an American singer and actress. She first gained recognition in 2011 when she began posting videos of herself covering popular songs online. One of her videos caught the attention of record producer <a href="/wiki/Dr._Luke" title="Dr. Luke">Dr. Luke</a>, who subsequently offered her a record deal with <a href="/wiki/Kemosabe_Records" title="Kemosabe Records">Kemosabe Records</a> in a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a>. While working on her debut effort, Gomez collaborated with artists <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cody_Simpson" title="Cody Simpson">Cody Simpson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cher_Lloyd" title="Cher Lloyd">Cher Lloyd</a>. In 2013, she released her debut commercial single, "<a href="/wiki/Jenny_from_the_Block#Cover_versions" title="Jenny from the Block">Becky from the Block</a>", to positive reception. Later that year, she released her debut extended play, <i><a href="/wiki/Play_It_Again_(EP)" title="Play It Again (EP)">Play It Again</a></i>. Her second single and first in 2014, "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Get_Enough_(Becky_G_song)" title="Can&#39;t Get Enough (Becky G song)">Can't Get Enough</a>", featured guest vocals from <a href="/wiki/Pitbull_(rapper)" title="Pitbull (rapper)">Pitbull</a> and went on to top the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Rhythm_Airplay" title="Latin Rhythm Airplay">Latin Rhythm Airplay</a> chart in the United States.
</p><p>Gomez achieved mainstream success with the release of "<a href="/wiki/Shower_(song)" title="Shower (song)">Shower</a>", that same year, which went on to enter the top twenty of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart. The single would go on to receive a multi platinum certification from the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), denoting two million units sold in the country. Following the success of "Shower", Gomez released "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Stop_Dancin%27_(Becky_G_song)" title="Can&#39;t Stop Dancin&#39; (Becky G song)">Can't Stop Dancin'</a>", "Lovin' So Hard" and "<a href="/wiki/Break_a_Sweat" title="Break a Sweat">Break a Sweat</a>" during 2014 and 2015, as singles from her then-forthcoming album. She embarked on a co-headlining tour with <a href="/wiki/J_Balvin" title="J Balvin">J Balvin</a> during September and October 2015, spanning throughout the United States. She portrayed Valentina Galindo in two episodes of the musical television series <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(2015_TV_series)" title="Empire (2015 TV series)">Empire</a></i>, contributing two new songs to the show's soundtrack. She released her first full-Spanish song "<a href="/wiki/Sola_(Becky_G_song)" title="Sola (Becky G song)">Sola</a>" in June 2016. In July 2018, Gomez released "Zooted" (featuring <a href="/wiki/French_Montana" title="French Montana">French Montana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Farruko" title="Farruko">Farruko</a>), as her first English-language song in three years. On September 27, 2019, she was featured on the "<a href="/wiki/Chicken_Noodle_Soup_(J-Hope_song)" title="Chicken Noodle Soup (J-Hope song)">Chicken Noodle Soup</a>" cover by South Korean rapper and dancer <a href="/wiki/J-Hope" title="J-Hope">J-Hope</a> of <a href="/wiki/BTS" title="BTS">BTS</a>. Her success has led her to collaborate with artists such as <a href="/wiki/Daddy_Yankee" title="Daddy Yankee">Daddy Yankee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Guetta" title="David Guetta">David Guetta</a>.
</p><p>Gomez's debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Mala_Santa" title="Mala Santa">Mala Santa</a></i>, released in October 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-idolator_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idolator-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> debuted at number 85 in the US <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">Billboard 200</a></i>, was certified 7× <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_certification" title="Music recording certification">platinum</a> by the RIAA Latin, debuted at number three in the <a href="/wiki/Top_Latin_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Latin Albums">Top Latin Albums</a>, and spawned the two <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_Latin_Songs" title="Hot Latin Songs">Hot Latin Songs</a> top-ten entries: "<a href="/wiki/Mayores" title="Mayores">Mayores</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Sin_Pijama" title="Sin Pijama">Sin Pijama</a>". Her May 2022 second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Esquemas" title="Esquemas">Esquemas</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> debuted at number 92 in the US, including number five on the Top Latin Albums, and debuted at number one in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Pop_Albums" title="Latin Pop Albums">Latin Pop Albums</a>; its third single, "<a href="/wiki/Mamiii" title="Mamiii">Mamiii</a>", became her highest-charting single in the US.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Becky_G" title="List of awards and nominations received by Becky G">Her accolades</a> include two <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, four <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">ASCAP Latin Awards</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Music_Awards" title="Latin American Music Awards">Latin American Music Awards</a>, plus the honorable Extraordinary Evolution Award, six <a href="/wiki/Premios_Juventud" title="Premios Juventud">Premios Juventud</a>, and four nominations from the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Grammy_Awards" title="Latin Grammy Awards">Latin Grammy Awards</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Becky_G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1997.E2.80.932011:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1997–2011:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings">1997–2011: Early life and career beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Becky_G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1997–2011: Early life and career beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
Rebbeca Marie Gomez<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21under21_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21under21-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> was born on March 2, 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-21under21_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21under21-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood, California</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FridaKahlo_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FridaKahlo-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> the oldest of four children, to <a href="/wiki/Mexican_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican American">Mexican American</a> parents Alejandra "Alex" (née Esquivias) and Francisco "Frank" Gomez.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mexican_roots_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mexican_roots-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> All four of her grandparents are from <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a>, Mexico, while her parents and most of her family were born in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Gomez has two brothers, and a younger sister.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In December 2017, she revealed she has a half-sister.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Gomez grew up in <a href="/wiki/Moreno_Valley,_California" title="Moreno Valley, California">Moreno Valley</a>, and at the age of nine her family lost their home and moved into the converted garage of her grandparents' house due to financial problems.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Gomez began working part-time jobs to help support her family, doing commercials and voice over work.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> She had what she described as a "mid-life crisis" when she was nine years old, and decided she wanted to pursue a music career.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> She was quoted as stating:<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>That was literally my mid-life crisis when I was nine years old. That's when I felt like, 'OK, I gotta get my life together. What am I gonna do?' I pushed that on myself at a younger age than the average kid because at the time my family had lost our home. I've always been more mature for my age, so I was already understanding what they were going through. And I just thought, 'How can I help them?'<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p> She initially attended public school, though had to undergo home schooling due to issues with bullying.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> She claimed that at one point she was jumped by multiple girls while in the restroom, and was a frequent target due to her jobs in the entertainment industry.<sup id="cite_ref-mtvbio_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvbio-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gomez appeared in the short film <i>El Tux</i> (2008) as Claudia Gómez and as Nina in the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Channel" title="Discovery Channel">Discovery Channel</a> television film <i><a href="/wiki/La_estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Calle_Olvera" title="La estación de la Calle Olvera">La estación de la Calle Olvera</a></i> (2008).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> She became a member of a girl group named G.L.A.M. in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and later joined B.C.G., a duo with G.L.A.M. member Cristal G.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  She filmed a music video as part of G.L.A.M. for a song titled "JellyBean" in 2009. During this time, Gomez also began recording herself singing and rapping songs using <a href="/wiki/Garageband" class="mw-redirect" title="Garageband">Garageband</a>, and created a YouTube account to post covers of popular songs online.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> She also began writing her own songs, and by the age of thirteen had taught herself how to play guitar.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Gomez befriended production duo The Jam when she was thirteen, who liked Gomez's written work.<sup id="cite_ref-mtvbio_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvbio-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The trio began working on material together, resulting in the covers of six songs: "<a href="/wiki/Otis_(song)" title="Otis (song)">Otis</a>", uploaded to YouTube on September 15, 2011, "<a href="/wiki/Lighters_(song)" title="Lighters (song)">Lighters</a>", released on October 13, "<a href="/wiki/Novacane_(song)" title="Novacane (song)">Novacane</a>", released on October 27, "<a href="/wiki/Take_Care_(song)" title="Take Care (song)">Take Care</a>", uploaded on March 1, 2012, "<a href="/wiki/Boyfriend_(Justin_Bieber_song)" title="Boyfriend (Justin Bieber song)">Boyfriend</a>", released on March 30, and the song "Turn the Music Up", a sample of "<a href="/wiki/Mi_Tierra_(song)" title="Mi Tierra (song)">Mi Tierra</a>", uploaded on July 18.<sup id="cite_ref-mtvbio_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvbio-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> These songs were meant to be part of a mixtape, titled <i>@itsbeckygomez</i>, though this project never came to fruition.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Her cover of "Otis" caught the attention of producer <a href="/wiki/Dr._Luke" title="Dr. Luke">Dr. Luke</a>, who had worked with artists including <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Luke scheduled a meeting with Gomez, and asked her to play guitar for him; he later signed her to his <a href="/wiki/Kemosabe_Records" title="Kemosabe Records">Kemosabe Records</a> record label, through <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mtvbio_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvbio-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In reference to her video clip for "Otis", Luke claimed "I would have signed her off that video alone. I was 100 percent in. She has so much personality and her voice just pops out of the speakers. Then I met her and discovered she could also sing and play the guitar and I thought, 'This is even better.' Then I found out she could write and it was like, 'What else are you going to tell me, that you're also Van Gogh?' Her potential is limitless."<sup id="cite_ref-mtvbio_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvbio-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after signing with the label, Gomez began work on her debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932015:_Commercial_success_with_music_and_acting"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2015:_Commercial_success_with_music_and_acting">2012–2015: Commercial success with music and acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Becky_G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2012–2015: Commercial success with music and acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Play_It_Again_(EP)" title="Play It Again (EP)">Play It Again (EP)</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Becky_G_performing_in_December_2013_in_Chicago_alt.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Becky_G_performing_in_December_2013_in_Chicago_alt.jpg/170px-Becky_G_performing_in_December_2013_in_Chicago_alt.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="231" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Becky_G_performing_in_December_2013_in_Chicago_alt.jpg/255px-Becky_G_performing_in_December_2013_in_Chicago_alt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Becky_G_performing_in_December_2013_in_Chicago_alt.jpg/340px-Becky_G_performing_in_December_2013_in_Chicago_alt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="884" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Becky G performing in 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>In August, while working on her debut album, Gomez released her first song, "Problem", featuring <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>, which was subsequently remixed into "Problem (The Monster Remix)" in September, for the <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Animation" title="Sony Pictures Animation">Sony Pictures Animation</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Hotel_Transylvania_(film)" title="Hotel Transylvania (film)">Hotel Transylvania</a></i>; the song served as a promotional single and also appeared in the movie's end credits.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Gomez and will.i.am filmed a music video for the song; it features Gomez wandering around a hotel with wil.i.am walking out of the walls while scenes from the movie also appear.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> She was featured on Australian singer <a href="/wiki/Cody_Simpson" title="Cody Simpson">Cody Simpson</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Wish_U_Were_Here" title="Wish U Were Here">Wish U Were Here</a>", serviced as the second single from his <a href="/wiki/Paradise_(Cody_Simpson_album)" title="Paradise (Cody Simpson album)">debut studio album</a> on August 7.<sup id="cite_ref-CSiTunes_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSiTunes-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> She worked with British singer <a href="/wiki/Cher_Lloyd" title="Cher Lloyd">Cher Lloyd</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/Oath_(song)" title="Oath (song)">Oath</a>", originally written by Gomez, released on October 2 as the fourth single from her <a href="/wiki/Sticks_and_Stones_(Cher_Lloyd_album)" title="Sticks and Stones (Cher Lloyd album)">debut album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The single had some commercial success, becoming Gomez's first song to chart on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The track was later certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), denoting sales of 500,000 copies in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She also worked with Brazilian singer <a href="/wiki/Michel_Tel%C3%B3" title="Michel Teló">Michel Teló</a> on a remix of his cover of the song "<a href="/wiki/Ai_Se_Eu_Te_Pego" title="Ai Se Eu Te Pego">Ai Se Eu Te Pego</a>", released on his UK EP on October 14. Four days later, Gomez uploaded a cover of American singer <a href="/wiki/Kesha" title="Kesha">Kesha</a>'s top ten single "<a href="/wiki/Die_Young" title="Die Young">Die Young</a>" on YouTube; portions of it were used in the official remix of the song which also featured American rappers <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, and was included on the Japanese deluxe edition of Kesha's second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Warrior_(Kesha_album)" title="Warrior (Kesha album)">Warrior</a></i> released the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 8, 2013, Gomez released "<a href="/wiki/Jenny_from_the_Block#Becky_G_(&quot;Becky_from_the_Block&quot;)" title="Jenny from the Block">Becky from the Block</a>" as her official debut single.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The song is a cover of American singer-actress <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>'s 2003 single "<a href="/wiki/Jenny_from_the_Block" title="Jenny from the Block">Jenny from the Block</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Gomez filmed a music video in her neighborhood, with Lopez herself making a cameo in the clip.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Tonight" title="Entertainment Tonight">Entertainment Tonight</a></i> described the version to have "give[n] Jenny's NY-based tune a West Coast slant".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Later, on May 6, Gomez released a new song, "Play It Again", for <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital download</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The track served as a promotional single, and was not an official single released by Gomez. On July 13, Gomez released her debut extended play, also titled <i><a href="/wiki/Play_It_Again_(EP)" title="Play It Again (EP)">Play It Again</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The album contained five songs on the standard edition, and its name was chosen by Gomez's fans. Gomez later filmed a music video for the song "Built For This", released on November 13, which she directed on her own. In October 2013 she confirmed that she was already recording her debut album. "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Get_Enough_(song_by_Becky_G)" class="mw-redirect" title="Can&#39;t Get Enough (song by Becky G)">Cant Get Enough</a>", which features a guest rap from American rapper <a href="/wiki/Pitbull_(rapper)" title="Pitbull (rapper)">Pitbull</a>, was serviced as the lead single from <i>Play It Again</i>, released on June 4, 2014. The song went on to top the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Rhythm_Airplay" title="Latin Rhythm Airplay">Latin Rhythm Airplay</a> chart in the United States, marking her first number one single on a <i>Billboard</i> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Spanglish and Spanish versions for "Play It Again" and "Can't Get Enough" were released to digital platforms in their respective years. Gomez performed the former on the <a href="/wiki/2013_Premios_Juventud" title="2013 Premios Juventud">2013 Premios Juventud</a> ceremony, where she was also nominated for "Revelación Juvenil" (<i>Young Revelation</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> She recorded the song "<a href="/wiki/Quiero_Bailar_(All_Through_the_Night)" title="Quiero Bailar (All Through the Night)">Quiero Bailar (All Through the Night)</a>" (2013) with Mexican DJ trio <a href="/wiki/3Ball_MTY" title="3Ball MTY">3Ball MTY</a>, which sees Gomez rapping and singing in both English and Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The song was used for their second studio album <i>Globall</i>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Becky_G_2014.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Becky_G_2014.png/170px-Becky_G_2014.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Becky_G_2014.png/255px-Becky_G_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Becky_G_2014.png/340px-Becky_G_2014.png 2x" data-file-width="695" data-file-height="900" /></a><figcaption>Becky G in 2014</figcaption></figure>
<p>Gomez released the song, "<a href="/wiki/Shower_(song)" title="Shower (song)">Shower</a>" as the initial lead single from her then upcoming English debut studio album on April 23, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The song proved to be a success for Gomez, reaching number 16 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The song achieved chart success in numerous other countries as well, most notably reaching number eleven in both Australia and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The single went on to receive a multi platinum certification from the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), denoting two million units sold in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-ShowerRIAA_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShowerRIAA-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Stop_Dancin%27_(Becky_G_song)" title="Can&#39;t Stop Dancin&#39; (Becky G song)">Can't Stop Dancin'</a>" was serviced as the next single from the album on November 4.<sup id="cite_ref-iTunes_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iTunes-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The song failed to match the success of her prior single, peaking at number 88 on the Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gomez opened for <a href="/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> on select dates of their <a href="/wiki/Demi_World_Tour" title="Demi World Tour">Demi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prismatic_World_Tour" title="Prismatic World Tour">Prismatic</a> world tours (2014–15) in both the United States and Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-NorthAmericaAnnounce_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorthAmericaAnnounce-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Gomez featured on the song "<a href="/wiki/Como_T%C3%BA_No_Hay_Dos_(song)" title="Como Tú No Hay Dos (song)">Como Tú No Hay Dos</a>" by Mexican singer-actress <a href="/wiki/Thal%C3%ADa" title="Thalía">Thalía</a>, released on January 7, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On March 3, she released a remix with Colombian reggaeton singer <a href="/wiki/J_Balvin" title="J Balvin">J Balvin</a> for "Can't Stop Dancin". she released a song titled "Lovin So Hard" on April 1, along with a music video consisting of homemade footage of Gomez and <a href="/wiki/Austin_Mahone" title="Austin Mahone">Austin Mahone</a>, whom she briefly dated.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On June 26, Gomez debuted a song titled "We Are Mexico" in solidarity with the Latin community in response to <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>'s remarks against illegal Mexican immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> She also performed at a tribute concert for the late Mexican-American singer <a href="/wiki/Jenni_Rivera" title="Jenni Rivera">Jenni Rivera</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Gomez appeared as Valentina Galindo in two episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(2015_TV_series)" title="Empire (2015 TV series)">Empire</a>,</i> performing the singles "Do It" and "New, New" for the show's soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> She released the song, "<a href="/wiki/Break_a_Sweat" title="Break a Sweat">Break a Sweat</a>" on August 20, the fourth single to be released from her then-album.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Gomez embarked on a co-headlining tour with Balvin beginning on September 23 and ending on October 25; the tour spanned across the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>  She later collaborated with Dutch DJs <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Claw_(DJs)" title="Yellow Claw (DJs)">Yellow Claw</a> on the songs "Wild Mustang" and "For the Thrill" from their album <i>Blood For Mercy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> She released "You Love It" on October 30, as a promotional single prior to the release of her debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> That same day, Gomez was cast as Trini in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Power_Rangers_(film)" title="Power Rangers (film)">Power Rangers</a></i> (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2016.E2.80.932018:_Crossover_to_Latin_music_and_films"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–2018:_Crossover_to_Latin_music_and_films">2016–2018: Crossover to Latin music and films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Becky_G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2016–2018: Crossover to Latin music and films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cast_of_the_Power_Rangers_movie_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Cast_of_the_Power_Rangers_movie_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Cast_of_the_Power_Rangers_movie_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Cast_of_the_Power_Rangers_movie_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Cast_of_the_Power_Rangers_movie_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Cast_of_the_Power_Rangers_movie_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Cast_of_the_Power_Rangers_movie_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="817" /></a><figcaption>Becky G with the cast of <i>Power Rangers</i></figcaption></figure>
<p>Gomez traveled to <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, Canada, to film <i><a href="/wiki/Power_Rangers_(film)" title="Power Rangers (film)">Power Rangers</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-collider1_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collider1-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Filming occurred from February 29 to May 28, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Gomez collaborated once more with Pitbull on the song "Superstar".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The song served as the official anthem for the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Am%C3%A9rica_Centenario" title="Copa América Centenario">Copa América Centenario</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Gomez decided to move to Spanish music in 2016, changing the course in her music career to the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_music_in_the_United_States" title="Latin American music in the United States">Latin music market</a>. On June 24, 2016, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/Sola_(Becky_G_song)" title="Sola (Becky G song)">Sola</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-sola_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sola-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The song serves as her first to be sung solely in Spanish and was planned to be the lead single from her then-upcoming Spanish debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-sola_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sola-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The song achieved success on Spanish radio, reaching number twenty-four on the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Pop_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin Pop Songs">Latin Pop Songs</a> chart in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> She featured alongside Puerto Rican singer <a href="/wiki/Yandel" title="Yandel">Yandel</a> in American rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Jon" title="Lil Jon">Lil Jon</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Take_It_Off_(Lil_Jon_song)" title="Take It Off (Lil Jon song)">Take It Off</a>", released on July 22, alongside its music video; a Spanglish version was released the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On October 7, Gomez released "<a href="/wiki/Mang%C3%BA_(Becky_G_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mangú (Becky G song)">Mangú</a>", her second Spanish song and follow-up to her single "Sola", after its premiere at the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Music_Awards_of_2016" title="Latin American Music Awards of 2016">Latin American Music Awards</a>. Gomez won the category for "Favorite Pop-Rock Female Artist" at the ceremony.
</p><p>Gomez was featured on American producers <a href="/wiki/Play-N-Skillz" title="Play-N-Skillz">Play-N-Skillz</a>'s both <a href="/wiki/Spanglish" title="Spanglish">Spanglish</a> and English remake versions of the 1994 song "<a href="/wiki/Si_Una_Vez#PlayNSkillsVersion" title="Si Una Vez">Si Una Vez</a>" by late Tejano singer <a href="/wiki/Selena" title="Selena">Selena</a>, alongside Mexican-American singer <a href="/wiki/Frankie_J" title="Frankie J">Frankie J</a> and American rapper <a href="/wiki/Kap_G" title="Kap G">Kap G</a>. The singles were released on February 24 and April 7, 2017, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On February 20, Gomez teased the release of her single, "<a href="/wiki/Todo_Cambio_(Becky_G_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Todo Cambio (Becky G song)">Todo Cambio</a>", after posting a photo of herself wearing a wedding dress on social media. The song was released on March 3, although its music video was filmed in Spain in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On March 24, <i>Power Rangers</i> was released, marking Gomez's feature film debut. She received public attention after it was revealed that her character, Trini, is queer, being the first <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">film superhero</a> to be from the <a href="/wiki/LGBT_community" title="LGBT community">LGBT community</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> She collaborated with Argentine singer <a href="/wiki/Axel_(singer)" title="Axel (singer)">Axel</a>, on the single "Que Nos Animemos", which was released on June 30, as part of his album <i>Ser.</i><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> On July 8, Gomez began a countdown on Twitter for her single "<a href="/wiki/Mayores" title="Mayores">Mayores</a>", with Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Bad_Bunny" title="Bad Bunny">Bad Bunny</a>. The song was released as the first single from her debut album on July 14.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Gomez stated that "Mayores" will mark the beginning of a "new era". The song became a mainstream success, reaching number one in Mexico, Spain, Romania, and nine Latin American countries, while reaching the top 10 in several others. It peaked at number three on <a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)"><i>Billboard</i></a>'s Hot Latin Songs chart and 74 on the Hot 100 chart, while also receiving a 46x platinum by the RIAA's Latin field.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Its music video reached 100 million views in one month and has achieved over 2 billion since 2021. On September 8, Gomez was featured on the song "Todo Lo Que Quiero" from Yandel's fourth solo studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Update_(Yandel_album)" title="Update (Yandel album)">#Update</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-itunes_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itunes-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On September 21, it was confirmed that Gomez would be the opening act for American girl group <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Harmony" title="Fifth Harmony">Fifth Harmony</a>, for the Latin American leg of their PSA Tour, with shows in Argentina, Chile, and Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> During the group's performance in Argentina, Gomez was pulled off the stage by security after being confused for a fan when attempting to cover member Dinah Jane with the country's flag when her outfit was ripping apart.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Gomez joined Dominican-American singer and long-time friend <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Grace" title="Leslie Grace">Leslie Grace</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/D%C3%ADganle" title="Díganle">Díganle</a>", released on September 28,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> which was remixed a year later with vocals from Latin boy band <a href="/wiki/CNCO" title="CNCO">CNCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Gomez also collaborated with American violinist <a href="/wiki/Lindsey_Stirling" title="Lindsey Stirling">Lindsey Stirling</a> as the featured vocalist on the track "Christmas C'mon", from Stirling's Christmas album, <i><a href="/wiki/Warmer_in_the_Winter" title="Warmer in the Winter">Warmer in the Winter</a></i>, released on October 20.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On October 26, she hosted along with Mexican actor <a href="/wiki/Diego_Boneta" title="Diego Boneta">Diego Boneta</a> the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Music_Awards_of_2017" title="Latin American Music Awards of 2017">Latin American Music Awards 2017</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Becky_G.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Becky_G.jpg/170px-Becky_G.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Becky_G.jpg/255px-Becky_G.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Becky_G.jpg/340px-Becky_G.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1333" data-file-height="2000" /></a><figcaption>Becky G in 2016</figcaption></figure>
<p>On February 9, 2018, Venezuelan duo <a href="/wiki/Mau_y_Ricky" title="Mau y Ricky">Mau y Ricky</a> released <a href="/wiki/Mi_Mala#Remix_version" title="Mi Mala">a remix</a> of their song "<a href="/wiki/Mi_Mala" title="Mi Mala">Mi Mala</a>" with Colombian singer <a href="/wiki/Karol_G" title="Karol G">Karol G</a> featuring Gomez, Grace and Argentine singer <a href="/wiki/Lali_Esp%C3%B3sito" title="Lali Espósito">Lali</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On the 16th of the same month, Jamaican rapper <a href="/wiki/Sean_Paul" title="Sean Paul">Sean Paul</a> and French DJ <a href="/wiki/David_Guetta" title="David Guetta">David Guetta</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Mad_Love_(Sean_Paul_and_David_Guetta_song)" title="Mad Love (Sean Paul and David Guetta song)">Mad Love</a>" also featuring Gomez, which was co-written by Colombian singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> and included on the EP <i><a href="/wiki/Mad_Love_the_Prequel" title="Mad Love the Prequel">Mad Love the Prequel</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On March 16, Spanish singer <a href="/wiki/Ana_Mena" title="Ana Mena">Ana Mena</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Ya_Es_Hora" title="Ya Es Hora">Ya Es Hora</a>" with Gomez and American singer <a href="/wiki/De_La_Ghetto" class="mw-redirect" title="De La Ghetto">De La Ghetto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> On April 20, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/Sin_Pijama" title="Sin Pijama">Sin Pijama</a>" with Dominican singer <a href="/wiki/Natti_Natasha" title="Natti Natasha">Natti Natasha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The song became another commercial success, peaking at number one in Bolivia, Chile, the Dominican Republic, El Salvador and Spain, reaching the top 10 of several countries in South America, peaking at number four on the Hot Latin Songs chart and at number 70 on the Hot 100. It received a Latin platinum certification in the U.S and reached 100 million views within three weeks of release; it has since achieved a 36x platinum certification and reached over 2 billion views on YouTube, being the most-viewed female collaboration on the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On April 27, Gomez was featured in a remix of "<a href="/wiki/Dura_(song)" title="Dura (song)">Dura</a>" by Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Daddy_Yankee" title="Daddy Yankee">Daddy Yankee</a>, alongside Bad Bunny and Natasha.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> They premiered the song as a surprise performance at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Billboard_Latin_Music_Awards" title="2018 Billboard Latin Music Awards">Billboard Latin Music Awards</a>. On June 15, Mau y Ricky released the song "Mal de la Cabeza" with Gomez, as a track from their album <i><a href="/wiki/Para_Aventuras_y_Curiosidades" title="Para Aventuras y Curiosidades">Para Aventuras y Curiosidades</a></i>; its title derives from the first line in the song.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Gomez returned to the English-speaking market after three years with the release of "Zooted" featuring Moroccan-American rapper <a href="/wiki/French_Montana" title="French Montana">French Montana</a> and Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Farruko" title="Farruko">Farruko</a>, which was made available for download on July 20. On August 2, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/Cuando_Te_Bes%C3%A9" title="Cuando Te Besé">Cuando Te Besé</a>" with Argentine rapper <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Londra" title="Paulo Londra">Paulo Londra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> It was certified 2x Latin platinum in the United States and is the first song to go number one on the <a href="/wiki/Argentina_Hot_100" title="Argentina Hot 100">Argentina Hot 100</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> A week later, Gomez starred in the sci-fi adventure film <a href="/wiki/A.X.L." title="A.X.L."><i>A.X.L</i>.</a>, which was filmed in late 2017; the movie received negative reviews from critics and, like <i>Power Rangers</i>, was a <a href="/wiki/Box-office_bomb" title="Box-office bomb">box-office disappointment</a>. Gomez starred in the lead role in the animated fantasy film <i><a href="/wiki/Gnome_Alone" title="Gnome Alone">Gnome Alone</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Josh_Peck" title="Josh Peck">Josh Peck</a>; it was originally slated for release in theaters, but was only released in Latin America, Europe and Asia in April 2018. It was made available in <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> on October of the same year. Gomez was honored by <a href="/wiki/The_Latin_Recording_Academy" title="The Latin Recording Academy">The Latin Recording Academy</a> as one of the <a href="/wiki/Leading_Ladies_of_Entertainment" title="Leading Ladies of Entertainment">Leading Ladies of Entertainment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-latinacademy_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latinacademy-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> On October 19, Mexican singer Joss Favela released the single "<a href="/wiki/Pienso_en_Ti_(Joss_Favela_and_Becky_G_song)" title="Pienso en Ti (Joss Favela and Becky G song)">Pienso en Ti</a>" with Gomez, which features <a href="/wiki/Regional_Mexican" title="Regional Mexican">Regional Mexican</a>, her first song in the genre.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, Spanish singer <a href="/wiki/C._Tangana" title="C. Tangana">C. Tangana</a> released the song "<a href="/wiki/Booty_(C._Tangana_and_Becky_G_song)" title="Booty (C. Tangana and Becky G song)">Booty</a>" with Gomez. The song peaked at number 3 in Spain and became the 93rd best-selling song in Spain in only two months. "Booty" was also certified double platinum in Spain and platinum in the United States. Its music video was nominated for Best Music Video at the <a href="/wiki/1st_Annual_Premios_Ode%C3%B3n" title="1st Annual Premios Odeón">2020 Premios Odeón</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> On October 25, 2018, Gomez, Mexican singer <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Trevi" title="Gloria Trevi">Gloria Trevi</a>, Grace, Puerto Rican actress <a href="/wiki/Roselyn_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Roselyn Sánchez">Roselyn Sánchez</a> and Mexican actress <a href="/wiki/Aracely_Ar%C3%A1mbula" title="Aracely Arámbula">Aracely Arámbula</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Music_Awards_of_2018" title="Latin American Music Awards of 2018">Latin American Music Awards 2018</a> in Los Angeles, California.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Gomez featured in "Lost in the Middle of Nowhere" from American singer <a href="/wiki/Kane_Brown" title="Kane Brown">Kane Brown</a>'s second album, <a href="/wiki/Experiment_(album)" title="Experiment (album)"><i>Experiment</i></a>. She featured on Puerto Rican producers DJ Luian and Mambo Kingz's single "<a href="/wiki/Bubalu" title="Bubalu">Bubalu</a>" featuring Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Anuel_AA" title="Anuel AA">Anuel AA</a> and American singer <a href="/wiki/Prince_Royce" title="Prince Royce">Prince Royce</a>. The single was released on November 6, 2018, and became a Top 30 hit on the Hot Latin Songs chart in the US, and has since been certified 21x platinum by the RIAA's Latin field.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On December 21, Gomez was featured in a remix of "<a href="/wiki/Mala_M%C3%ADa" title="Mala Mía">Mala Mía</a>" by Colombian singer <a href="/wiki/Maluma" title="Maluma">Maluma</a>, alongside Brazilian singer <a href="/wiki/Anitta_(singer)" title="Anitta (singer)">Anitta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2019.E2.80.932021:_Mala_Santa"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–2021:_Mala_Santa">2019–2021: <i>Mala Santa</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Becky_G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2019–2021: Mala Santa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mala_Santa" title="Mala Santa">Mala Santa</a></div>
<p>On January 18, 2019, Gomez officially made her return to English music with the release of "LBD", along with its lyric video.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> On March 1, Gomez performed a series of shows in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, starting with a headlining set at the <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B1a_del_Mar_International_Song_Festival" title="Viña del Mar International Song Festival">Viña del Mar International Song Festival</a> festival in <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B1a_del_Mar" title="Viña del Mar">Viña del Mar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> On March 22, she released her next single "Green Light Go" to digital download and streaming.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Gomez embarked on her self-titled tour, visiting Spanish-speaking countries.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> On March 28, Kane Brown released a Spanish version of "Lost in the Middle of Nowhere" with Gomez, along with a music video, and a behind-the-scenes clip with the English version.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Gomez featured on Anitta's single "<a href="/wiki/Banana_(Anitta_song)" title="Banana (Anitta song)">Banana</a>", released on April 5, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On April 19, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/La_Respuesta" title="La Respuesta">La Respuesta</a>" with Maluma.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> On April 26, Gomez released the single "Next to You" with British DJ <a href="/wiki/Digital_Farm_Animals" title="Digital Farm Animals">Digital Farm Animals</a> and Jamaican producer <a href="/wiki/Rvssian" title="Rvssian">Rvssian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> "Un Mundo Ideal", a bilingual version of "<a href="/wiki/A_Whole_New_World" title="A Whole New World">A Whole New World</a>", was performed by English singer <a href="/wiki/Zayn_Malik" title="Zayn Malik">Zayn Malik</a> and Gomez for <a href="/wiki/Aladdin_(2019_soundtrack)" title="Aladdin (2019 soundtrack)">the soundtrack</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Aladdin_(2019_film)" title="Aladdin (2019 film)">2019 remake of <i>Aladdin</i></a>. The song was released on May 17, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On May 24, Gomez with Digital Farm Animals and Rvssian released a remix of "Next to You" featuring Nigerian-American singer <a href="/wiki/Davido" title="Davido">Davido</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> On June 28, Colombian group <a href="/wiki/ChocQuibTown" title="ChocQuibTown">ChocQuibTown</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Que_Me_Baile" title="Que Me Baile">Que Me Baile</a>" with Gomez.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> She collaborated with Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Myke_Towers" title="Myke Towers">Myke Towers</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/Dollar_(song)" title="Dollar (song)">Dollar</a>" which was released on July 10.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> On July 12, Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Guaynaa" title="Guaynaa">Guaynaa</a> released <a href="/wiki/Rebota#Remix_version" title="Rebota">a remix</a> of his song "<a href="/wiki/Rebota" title="Rebota">Rebota</a>" with American singer <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Jam" title="Nicky Jam">Nicky Jam</a> and Farruko featuring Gomez and Panamanian singer <a href="/wiki/Sech_(singer)" title="Sech (singer)">Sech</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> On September 6, Senegalese-American singer <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a> released "<a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3mo_No" title="Cómo No">Cómo No</a>" featuring Gomez, as the lead single from his album <i><a href="/wiki/El_Negreeto" title="El Negreeto">El Negreeto</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On September 13, Gomez released the single "Secrets".<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> On September 20, American rapper <a href="/wiki/Saweetie" title="Saweetie">Saweetie</a> released "<a href="/wiki/My_Type_(Saweetie_song)" title="My Type (Saweetie song)">My Type (Latin Remix)</a>" featuring Gomez and Dominican rapper Meliii.<sup id="cite_ref-remix2_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-remix2-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> On September 27, she featured on South Korean rapper <a href="/wiki/J-Hope" title="J-Hope">J-Hope</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Chicken_Noodle_Soup_(J-Hope_song)" title="Chicken Noodle Soup (J-Hope song)">Chicken Noodle Soup</a>". The song contains lyrics in Spanish, English, and Korean, written by both in their respective languages. The music video for the song featured 50 dancers of different nationalities.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> That same day, she was appeared on Pitbull's eleventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Libertad_548" title="Libertad 548">Libertad 548</a></i>, on the track "Mala".
</p><p>Gomez announced her debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Mala_Santa" title="Mala Santa">Mala Santa</a></i> on October 8, 2019, calling it a "new era". She released <a href="/wiki/Mala_Santa_(song)" title="Mala Santa (song)">title track</a> as the fifth single on October 11, along with a visual released on YouTube. <i>Mala Santa</i> was released on October 17, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-idolator_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idolator-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The record includes new collaborations with Sech, Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Darell_(rapper)" title="Darell (rapper)">Darell</a>, Mau y Ricky, American singer <a href="/wiki/Dalex" title="Dalex">Dalex</a>, Puerto Rican duo <a href="/wiki/Zion_%26_Lennox" title="Zion &amp; Lennox">Zion &amp; Lennox</a> and Farruko; each track had visuals which were released on YouTube on the same day of the album, except the previously released singles. She performed "Dollar" with Towers at the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Music_Awards_of_2019" title="Latin American Music Awards of 2019">Latin American Music Awards</a> the same day, and later performed a medley of "Mayores", "Sin Pijama" and "Mala Santa", after which Gomez was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Music_Awards_of_2019" title="Latin American Music Awards of 2019">Extraordinary Evolution Award</a> for her evolving work in a short span of years.<sup id="cite_ref-extraordinaryevolutionaward_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extraordinaryevolutionaward-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The album received acclaim from music critics and debuted in the top five of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Top_Latin_Albums" title="Billboard Top Latin Albums"><i>Billboard</i> Top Latin Albums</a> and 85 of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>On November 3, she hosted in the <a href="/wiki/2019_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="2019 MTV Europe Music Awards">2019 MTV Europe Music Awards</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-host_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-host-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> On November 10, Gomez was part of the song "Giants", as Qiyana, by virtual hip-hop group True Damage in <i><a href="/wiki/League_of_Legends" title="League of Legends">League of Legends</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/2019_League_of_Legends_World_Championship" title="2019 League of Legends World Championship">2019 World Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> On the same day, she was part of its live performance for the opening ceremony of the finals.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>On January 31, 2020, Mexican pop singer <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Rivera" title="Carlos Rivera">Carlos Rivera</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Perdiendo_la_Cabeza" title="Perdiendo la Cabeza">Perdiendo la Cabeza</a>" with Gomez and Puerto Rican singer <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Cap%C3%B3" title="Pedro Capó">Pedro Capó</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> On March 20, Gomez was featured in a remix of "Boys Ain't Shit" by Australian singer <a href="/wiki/Saygrace" title="Saygrace">Saygrace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> On April 13, Gomez released the single "They Ain't Ready".<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> On April 23, Cuban reggaeton duo <a href="/wiki/Gente_de_Zona" title="Gente de Zona">Gente de Zona</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Muchacha_(song)" title="Muchacha (song)">Muchacha</a>" with Gomez.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> On May 28, Mexican-American singer <a href="/wiki/Chiquis_Rivera" title="Chiquis Rivera">Chiquis</a> and Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/Jolene_(song)" title="Jolene (song)">Jolene</a>" a <a href="/wiki/Cumbia" title="Cumbia">cumbia</a> style Spanish-language cover of American singer <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>'s song.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> On June 19, Gomez was featured on the song "Duro Hard" from American hip-hop group <a href="/wiki/Black_Eyed_Peas" title="Black Eyed Peas">Black Eyed Peas</a> Latin album <i><a href="/wiki/Translation_(album)" title="Translation (album)">Translation</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> On June 19, Spanish singer <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Mateo" title="Abraham Mateo">Abraham Mateo</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Tiempo_Pa_Olvidar" title="Tiempo Pa Olvidar">Tiempo Pa Olvidar</a>" with Gomez.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> On July 10, Gomez released the single "My Man", and its video-game inspired music video features her and boyfriend <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Lletget" title="Sebastian Lletget">Sebastian Lletget</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> On July 17, Pitbull released the remix to "Mala", with additional guest vocals from De La Ghetto.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> On September 3, Juhn released the single "Otro Día Lluvioso" with Puerto Rican singer <a href="/wiki/Dyland_%26_Lenny" title="Dyland &amp; Lenny">Lenny Tavárez</a> and Gomez featuring Dalex.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> On October 9, she was featured in a remix of "<a href="/wiki/Latina_(Reykon_song)" title="Latina (Reykon song)">Latina</a>" by Colombian singers <a href="/wiki/Reykon" title="Reykon">Reykon</a> and Maluma, alongside American rapper <a href="/wiki/Tyga" title="Tyga">Tyga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> On October 29, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/No_Drama_(Becky_G_and_Ozuna_song)" title="No Drama (Becky G and Ozuna song)">No Drama</a>" with Puerto Rican singer <a href="/wiki/Ozuna" title="Ozuna">Ozuna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> On December 10, she was featured in a remix of "<a href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9_Maldici%C3%B3n" title="Qué Maldición">Qué Maldición</a>" by Mexican group <a href="/wiki/Banda_MS" title="Banda MS">Banda MS</a> and American rapper <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> On December 18, she was featured in a remix of "La Curiosidad" by Puerto Rican singers <a href="/wiki/Jay_Wheeler" title="Jay Wheeler">Jay Wheeler</a> and Towers alongside American rapper <a href="/wiki/Arc%C3%A1ngel" title="Arcángel">Arcángel</a>, Zion &amp; Lennox, De La Ghetto and Puerto Rican rapper Brray.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 22, 2021, Gomez released the single "Rotate" with Nigerian singer <a href="/wiki/Burna_Boy" title="Burna Boy">Burna Boy</a>. The song was used in <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> commercials featuring soccer players, including <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> On March, she made a cameo in Natasha's music video for "Las Nenas".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> On March 4, Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Kevvo" title="Kevvo">Kevvo</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Te_Va_Bien" title="Te Va Bien">Te Va Bien</a>" with Arcángel and Gomez featuring Darell.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> On March 5, Gomez collaborated with Puerto Rican record producer <a href="/wiki/Tainy" title="Tainy">Tainy</a> and American singer <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Daniel_(singer)" title="Trevor Daniel (singer)">Trevor Daniel</a> on "F is For Friends" for <i><a href="/wiki/The_SpongeBob_Movie:_Sponge_on_the_Run" title="The SpongeBob Movie: Sponge on the Run">The SpongeBob Movie: Sponge on the Run</a></i> soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> On April 14, American R&amp;B and pop group <a href="/wiki/Emotional_Oranges" title="Emotional Oranges">Emotional Oranges</a> released the single "Down to Miami" featuring Gomez.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On April 20, Natasha released the single "<a href="/wiki/Ram_Pam_Pam" title="Ram Pam Pam">Ram Pam Pam</a>" with Gomez, as a single for both of their second studio albums.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> They premiered the song on American television on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a></i> on May 17, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> On June 4, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/Fulanito_(song)" title="Fulanito (song)">Fulanito</a>" in collaboration with Dominican rapper <a href="/wiki/El_Alfa" title="El Alfa">El Alfa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> On July 15, Argentine rapper <a href="/wiki/Khea" title="Khea">Khea</a> released the single "Only One" with Gomez and American singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Julia_Michaels" title="Julia Michaels">Julia Michaels</a> featuring Jamaican songwriter and producer <a href="/wiki/Di_Genius" title="Di Genius">Di Genius</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On August 26, Argentine singer <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Becerra" title="María Becerra">María Becerra</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Wow_Wow" title="Wow Wow">Wow Wow</a>" featuring Gomez, included on Becerra's studio album <a href="/wiki/Animal_(Mar%C3%ADa_Becerra_album)" title="Animal (María Becerra album)"><i>Animal</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> On September 10, Mexican singer <a href="/wiki/Sof%C3%ADa_Reyes" title="Sofía Reyes">Sofía Reyes</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Mal_de_Amores" title="Mal de Amores">Mal de Amores</a>" with Gomez, as the lead single of Reyes's second studio album of the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> On September 16, Play-N-Skillz released the single "<a href="/wiki/Baila_As%C3%AD" title="Baila Así">Baila Así</a>" with Gomez, Thalía and Chiquis.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> On October 22, American singer <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Pa_Mis_Muchachas" title="Pa Mis Muchachas">Pa Mis Muchachas</a>" with Gomez and Argentine rapper <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Nicole" title="Nicki Nicole">Nicki Nicole</a>, featuring Argentine singer <a href="/wiki/Nathy_Peluso" title="Nathy Peluso">Nathy Peluso</a>, which served as the lead single from her <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/La_Fuerza" title="La Fuerza">La Fuerza</a></i> and part of her album <i><a href="/wiki/Aguilera_(album)" title="Aguilera (album)">Aguilera</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> 
For her work on the album as a featured artist on the track, she was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Latin_Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Latin Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a> at the <a href="/wiki/23rd_Annual_Latin_Grammy_Awards" title="23rd Annual Latin Grammy Awards">23rd Annual Latin Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In November 2021, Gomez began hosting her own <a href="/wiki/Facebook_Watch" title="Facebook Watch">Facebook Watch</a> talk show, titled <i>Face to Face with Becky G</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_FaceToFace_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_FaceToFace-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Her first guest was American singer <a href="/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_FaceToFace_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_FaceToFace-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> On November 26, Gomez released song "Lo Que Yo Diga" from the <i>Koati</i> film soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> On December 1, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/Bella_Ciao_(Becky_G_song)" title="Bella Ciao (Becky G song)">Bella Ciao</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2022.E2.80.93present:_Esquemas_and_Esquinas"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2022–present:_Esquemas_and_Esquinas">2022–present: <i>Esquemas</i> and <i>Esquinas</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Becky_G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2022–present: Esquemas and Esquinas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Esquemas" title="Esquemas">Esquemas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Esquinas_(album)" title="Esquinas (album)">Esquinas (album)</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Becky_G_MIAW.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Becky_G_MIAW.jpg/220px-Becky_G_MIAW.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Becky_G_MIAW.jpg/330px-Becky_G_MIAW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Becky_G_MIAW.jpg/440px-Becky_G_MIAW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1112" data-file-height="710" /></a><figcaption>Becky G in 2022</figcaption></figure>
<p>In February 2022, Gomez released "<a href="/wiki/Mamiii" title="Mamiii">Mamiii</a>" with Karol G as the third single from her second studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The song debuted at number 15 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and peaking at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Latin_Songs" title="Hot Latin Songs">Hot Latin Songs</a>, becoming Gomez highest-charting song. The song received nominations for the Favorite Latin Song at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2022" title="American Music Awards of 2022">American Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Hot Latin Song of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/2022_Billboard_Latin_Music_Awards" title="2022 Billboard Latin Music Awards">Billboard Latin Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Best Urban Song at the <a href="/wiki/23rd_Annual_Latin_Grammy_Awards" title="23rd Annual Latin Grammy Awards">Latin Grammy Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Best Latin at the <a href="/wiki/2022_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2022 MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and won for the Viral Anthem at the <a href="/wiki/2022_MTV_MIAW_Awards" title="2022 MTV MIAW Awards">MTV MIAW Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Girl Power at the <a href="/wiki/2022_Premios_Juventud" title="2022 Premios Juventud">Premios Juventud</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Collaboration of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/2022_Premios_Tu_M%C3%BAsica_Urbano" title="2022 Premios Tu Música Urbano">Premios Tu Música Urbano</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Latin Pop/Reggaeton Song of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/2023_iHeartRadio_Music_Awards" title="2023 iHeartRadio Music Awards">iHeartRadio Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Song of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Music_Awards_of_2023" title="Latin American Music Awards of 2023">Latin American Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Song of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/Premio_Lo_Nuestro_2023" title="Premio Lo Nuestro 2023">Lo Nuestro Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In March 2022, Gomez joined American singer <a href="/wiki/Joe_Jonas" title="Joe Jonas">Joe Jonas</a> and American choreographer <a href="/wiki/Sean_Bankhead_(choreographer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Bankhead (choreographer)">Sean Bankhead</a> to serve as judges on the <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/TikTok" title="TikTok">TikTok</a> American music competition series <i><a href="/wiki/Becoming_a_Popstar" title="Becoming a Popstar">Becoming a Popstar</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> On March 24, Gomez alongside Natasha were featured on the song "<a href="/wiki/Zona_del_Perreo" title="Zona del Perreo">Zona del Perreo</a>" from Daddy Yankee's last studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Legendaddy_(album)" title="Legendaddy (album)">Legendaddy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Gomez released "<a href="/wiki/No_Mienten" title="No Mienten">No Mienten</a>" on April 20, as the fourth single from her second album.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> On April 28, Regional Mexican group Marca MP released the single "<a href="/wiki/Ya_Acab%C3%B3" title="Ya Acabó">Ya Acabó</a>" with Gomez.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> She released "<a href="/wiki/Bail%C3%A9_Con_Mi_Ex" title="Bailé Con Mi Ex">Bailé Con Mi Ex</a>" on May 10 as the album's fifth and final single along with its music video.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>  Gomez released her second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Esquemas" title="Esquemas">Esquemas</a></i>, on May 13.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number 92 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, including number 5 on the <a href="/wiki/Top_Latin_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Latin Albums">Top Latin Albums</a> and number 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Pop_Albums" title="Latin Pop Albums">Latin Pop Albums</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bustios_Bustios_2022_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bustios_Bustios_2022-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The record featured new collaborations with American-Venezuelan singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Elena_Rose" title="Elena Rose">Elena Rose</a> and Guaynaa. Gomez starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Machine_Gun_Kelly_(musician)" title="Machine Gun Kelly (musician)">Machine Gun Kelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mod_Sun" title="Mod Sun">Mod Sun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dove_Cameron" title="Dove Cameron">Dove Cameron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megan_Fox" title="Megan Fox">Megan Fox</a> in the film <a href="/wiki/Good_Mourning_(film)" title="Good Mourning (film)"><i>Good Mourning</i></a>, released on May 22. On July 6, Argentine singer <a href="/wiki/Tini_(singer)" title="Tini (singer)">Tini</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/La_Loto" title="La Loto">La Loto</a>", a collaboration with Gomez and Anitta, which serves as the seventh single from Tini's fourth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Cupido_(album)" title="Cupido (album)">Cupido</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> On July 10, she hosted with Mexican TikTok star Jimena Jiménez in the <a href="/wiki/2022_MTV_Millennial_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2022 MTV Millennial Awards">2022 MTV Millennial Awards</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> On September 16, Gomez released the single "<a href="/wiki/Amantes_(song)" title="Amantes (song)">Amantes</a>" with Spanish singer Daviles de Novelda, which features <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(music)" title="Bachata (music)">bachata music</a>, her first song in the genre.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> On October 13, Gomez appeared alongside Colombian singer <a href="/wiki/Greeicy_Rend%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Greeicy Rendón">Greeicy</a>, Becerra, and Tini on a remix of Rose's song "La Ducha".<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Gomez was also named to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>'</i> <a href="/wiki/30_Under_30" class="mw-redirect" title="30 Under 30">30 Under 30</a> list in the music category.<sup id="cite_ref-forbeslist_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbeslist-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 14, 2023, Mexican regional quartet <a href="/wiki/Fuerza_Regida" title="Fuerza Regida">Fuerza Regida</a> released the single "<a href="/wiki/Te_Quiero_Besar" title="Te Quiero Besar">Te Quiero Besar</a>" with Gomez.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> On March 1, she received the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music#Impact_Award" title="Billboard Women in Music">Impact Award</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music" title="Billboard Women in Music"><i>Billboard</i> Women in Music</a> event.<sup id="cite_ref-billboardimpact_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboardimpact-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> On March 10, she released the single "<a href="/wiki/Arranca" title="Arranca">Arranca</a>" featuring Dominican singer <a href="/wiki/Omega_(singer)" title="Omega (singer)">Omega</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> On March 30, she released the single "<a href="/wiki/Chanel_(Becky_G_and_Peso_Pluma_song)" title="Chanel (Becky G and Peso Pluma song)">Chanel</a>" with Mexican singer <a href="/wiki/Peso_Pluma" title="Peso Pluma">Peso Pluma</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:28_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:28-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> as the first single for her upcoming regional Mexican album.
